    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer5938571077430531087">From the author of <i>The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley </i>comes a brand-new novel about a teenage boy who must decide whether or not the world is worth saving.<br/><br/>Henry Denton has spent years being periodically abducted by aliens. Then the aliens give him an ultimatum: The world will end in 144 days, and all Henry has to do to stop it is push a big red button.<br/><br/>Only he isn’t sure he </span>
  <span id="freeText5938571077430531087" style="display:none">From the author of <i>The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley </i>comes a brand-new novel about a teenage boy who must decide whether or not the world is worth saving.<br /><br />Henry Denton has spent years being periodically abducted by aliens. Then the aliens give him an ultimatum: The world will end in 144 days, and all Henry has to do to stop it is push a big red button.<br /><br />Only he isn’t sure he wants to.<br /><br />After all, life hasn’t been great for Henry. His mom is a struggling waitress held together by a thin layer of cigarette smoke. His brother is a jobless dropout who just knocked someone up. His grandmother is slowly losing herself to Alzheimer’s. And Henry is still dealing with the grief of his boyfriend’s suicide last year.<br /><br />Wiping the slate clean sounds like a pretty good choice to him.<br /><br />But Henry is a scientist first, and facing the question thoroughly and logically, he begins to look for pros and cons: in the bully who is his perpetual one-night stand, in the best friend who betrayed him, in the brilliant and mysterious boy who walked into the wrong class. Weighing the pain and the joy that surrounds him, Henry is left with the ultimate choice: push the button and save the planet and everyone on it…or let the world—and his pain—be destroyed forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5938571077430531087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1503480390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1684847111235930786"><blockquote>
  <i>Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe.<br/>But you don't.<br/>Because we are the ants.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>My first 5 stars of 2016!</b><br/><br/>This book. Seriously. I hadn't read any of the author's other work. I wasn't even sure that the premise promised a book I would like. My curiosity was piqued when I saw the good critical reviews it was getting, but that has meant little in the past so I wasn't completely convinced...<br/><br/><b>But it was so damn good</b>. The truth is</span>
  <span id="freeText1684847111235930786" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe.<br />But you don't.<br />Because we are the ants.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>My first 5 stars of 2016!</b><br /><br />This book. Seriously. I hadn't read any of the author's other work. I wasn't even sure that the premise promised a book I would like. My curiosity was piqued when I saw the good critical reviews it was getting, but that has meant little in the past so I wasn't completely convinced...<br /><br /><b>But it was so damn good</b>. The truth is, while I always wait for the end before deciding on a book rating, most of the time there's a little part of me that <i>just knows</i> near the beginning when I've picked up a 5-star book. It's a book that does something a bit different, and it has a pull you know will drag you through those pages.<br /><br />Henry Denton's narrative is so compelling, nihilistic and hilarious. He's a smart, witty and very funny human being, prone to one tragic misfortune after another. The way he portrays and explores the world around him is excellent, showing us intricate family bonds, friendships, love and all the wonder and horror of the world we live in.<br /><br />The book opens with Henry telling us about the aliens. The aliens who have abducted him several times, conducted experiments on him, and finally given him the ultimate choice. The world is going to end, but pushing a button will stop it - will Henry find reason to save the world?<br /><br />In the wrong hands, it could have been unbearably cheesy, but the tone is just right. Dark, but often comical. Sad, but full of heart-warming moments too. <br /><br />The description gives the impression that Henry meets Diego and his perspective on life changes, but it's far more complex than that. <b>This book is not a romance, and so many characters have an important part to play in the telling of the story</b>: Henry's ex-boyfriend who committed suicide, his alcoholic wannabe-chef mother, the popular boy who makes out with him one minute and bullies him the next, his grandmother with Alzheimer's, his college-dropout brother, as well as others.<br /><br />All the characters are so well-developed, all are complex, none are throwaway. Hutchinson weaves relationships gradually, throughout the novel, showing all the layers that exist underneath the surface and - ultimately - showing that every person has more than one side, is more than one thing.<br /><br />It's the kind of truly smart and insightful book that doesn't come along too often. And it left my mind spinning with thoughts long after I finished the last page.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1684847111235930786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1430253248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430253248" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430253248?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430253248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2033333585294943267"><i>"I could paint you sometime."<br/>"I'm afraid to ask what you see when you look at me."<br/>"You wouldn't believe me."</i><br/><br/>This was my second book by Shaun David Hutchinson and I loved it even more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20500616.The_Five_Stages_of_Andrew_Brawley' title='The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley by Shaun David Hutchinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley</a>. It deals with several heavy topics like depression, Alzheimers, suicide and bullying, as well as science, family, love and friendship, a combination that works perfectly.<br/><br/><b>Characters:</b><br/><i>We are the Ants</i> is very raw and real, and it has everything to do with its characters. They are </span>
  <span id="freeText2033333585294943267" style="display:none"><i>"I could paint you sometime."<br />"I'm afraid to ask what you see when you look at me."<br />"You wouldn't believe me."</i><br /><br />This was my second book by Shaun David Hutchinson and I loved it even more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20500616.The_Five_Stages_of_Andrew_Brawley" title="The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley by Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley</a>. It deals with several heavy topics like depression, Alzheimers, suicide and bullying, as well as science, family, love and friendship, a combination that works perfectly.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br /><i>We are the Ants</i> is very raw and real, and it has everything to do with its characters. They are all broken somehow, and so precious at the same time. Everyone of them copes with reality in a different way, some better than others. All of them have this character-depth and grow throughout the story. Even and especially Henry's brother, who I hated in the beginning, but went through the most surprising changes. I also fell in love with Audrey and Diego, Henry's closest friends, as well as Mrs. Faraci, his teacher.<br /><br /><b>Writing:</b><br />I just love the writing. It's beautiful and smart and brought me to tears. There is so much truth in SDH's words. I hope he never stops writing. Here are a few of my favourite quotes:<br /><br /><i>“Dreams are hopeful because they exist as pure possibility. Unlike memories, which are fossils, long dead and buried deep.”</i><br /><br /><i>“Sometimes I think gravity may be death in disguise. Other times I think gravity is love, which is why love's only demand is that we fall.”</i><br /><br /><i>“You spend your life hoarding memories against the day you'll lack the energy to go out and make new ones, because that's the comfort of the old age. The ability to look back at your life and know that you left your mark on the world. But I'm losing my memories, it's like someone's broken into my piggy bank and is robbing me one penny at a time. It's happening so slowly, I can hardly tell what's missing.”</i><br /><br /><b>Plot:</b><br />I wasn't surprised to find this book to be even darker than <i>The Five Stages of Andrew Brawley</i>. What shocked me most was the violence in Henry's family and the bullying he suffers at school. Bullying sucks. And with everything that drags Henry down already, I'm still surprised he didn't break completely after what happened to him. Henry gets publicly shamed, insulted and disrespected in the most horrible ways. That's what broke me inside. I really felt for him in those moments, it made me unbearably angry and sad.<br />The only thing that bugged me was the aliens, the abductions and every single time I stumbled on the word <i>slugger</i>. It made me cringe. Henry really had enough problems, vanishing for days and the turning up in strange places, without clothes or memories of how he got there, was something he could have done without.<br /><br /><b>Feminism and Sexuality:</b><br />This book has some messages. They're not obvious or loud, but they're subtle. It made me so happy. There was no coming out scene. In an ideal world nobody has to "come out". The baby's room wasn't painted in pink just because it was a girl. In an ideal world nobody forces colours to be gender-specified. The principal, physics teacher and police officer weren't all white and male. In an ideal world positions of power are equally represented by all genders and races.<br /><br />Thank you for this incredibly honest novel. I'm looking forward to S. H. Hutchinson's future projects.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2033333585294943267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2407999249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407999249" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407999249?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/26560207-gabby">Gabby</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=pan">pan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407999249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3003219986080001316"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527713793i/25623369._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“We may not get to choose how we die, but we can choose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>We Are the Ants</i> is a really beautiful story about being a teenager, being gay, and not being accepted. This is a story about heartbreak, loss, grief, and trying to figure out who you are in the midst of it all. I’ll be honest, I didn’t love the start of this book, but I completely fell in love with the middle and </span>
  <span id="freeText3003219986080001316" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527713793i/25623369._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“We may not get to choose how we die, but we can choose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>We Are the Ants</i> is a really beautiful story about being a teenager, being gay, and not being accepted. This is a story about heartbreak, loss, grief, and trying to figure out who you are in the midst of it all. I’ll be honest, I didn’t love the start of this book, but I completely fell in love with the middle and end. And I totally understand why so many of my friends hail this as their favorite book of all time. <br><br>But the reason I’m giving this four stars is because the first part of this book felt just so vulgar. Like, maybe it’s because I’m a grown woman and I don’t want to read about teenage boners, but like the first part of this book just reads crude and bad. I was honestly scared I was going to end up hating this book. Which would have really surprised me, because Shaun David Hutchinson’s short story in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193748272" rel="nofollow noopener">All Out Anthology</a> was my favorite in the entire collection. It was so beautifully written, so lyrical, so immersive, so empowering. And luckily for me, I didn’t give up hope, because <i>We Are the Ants</i> ended up being all of those things, too. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That's the problem with memories: you can visit them, but you can't live in them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book stars a young boy named Henry who is grieving the loss of his boyfriend who recently committed suicide. His home situation isn’t great either, from a mom that is also unhappy, a brother that is abusive and making some big life changes, and a grandmother who can hardly remember his name. Also, Henry is the joke of his high school and has been dubbed “Space Boy” because he frequently gets abducted by aliens, regardless of who believes him or not. <br><br>We get to witness some of Henry’s alien abductions, but on one particular visit, he is given a choice to save the world or to leave it for impending destruction. Henry has 144 days to decide if the world is worth saving. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If you knew the world was going to end, and you could press a button to prevent it, would you?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book does deal with so many heavy topics, so please use caution and make sure you are in the right mindset. <b>Trigger and content warnings</b> for attempted rape, sexual assault, outing, suicide, a lot of physical abuse, extreme bullying, homophobia, homophobic slurs, drug addiction, alcoholism, grief, depression, abandonment, loss of a loved one, talk of self-harm/cutting, and having a loved one with Alzheimer's disease. <br><br>Another important aspect I love in this book was the depictions of adults. First off, Henry’s mother is dealing with so many things, and so much heartache of her own, and she doesn’t hide it. I’m not saying everything she did was healthy, but it's realistic and I think it’s something really important for more teens to read and see that they aren’t alone. High key, Ms. Faraci was my favorite character. I seriously loved that teacher and her honest advice that sometimes awful people do indeed succeed in the world, but it doesn’t mean that they will always be in your life. I also just loved seeing a teacher care about a student the way that she did with Henry. It was truly heartwarming and meant a lot to me. <br><br>Another really real and raw theme of the book is how we use other people to fill a void left by someone else. And how we will make excuses and justifications for the only person who is making us feel something, even if they are abusive and manipulative. This just really spoke to my soul, honestly. <br><br>I wouldn’t say that this book is about romance, but there is a romance element and let me climb up on the rooftops and scream that <b>the love interest in this book is a Latinx Pansexual boy</b>! You all, I was not expecting pan rep in this book, and even though the actual word is not on the page, my heart was so damn happy. <br><br>Overall, Shaun David Hutchinson has now impressed me twice in 2018 and I’m no longer going to sleep on his work. I think he’s so immensely talented, and all the elements that are a part of his stories are honestly life changing and saving. And I hope you all might consider picking up <i>We Are the Ants</i> and get blown away, too. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Depression isn't a war you win. It's a battle you fight every day. You never stop, never get to rest. It's one bloody fray after another.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>This story is truly holds such an important discussion about mental illness and how it is something that you have to always manage and keep up with, because it never goes away, no matter how many alien abductions happen. And I’m going to leave some numbers here:<br><br>➽<b>SUICIDE PREVENTION:</b><br>National Suicide Prevention Lifeline: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://suicidepreventionlifeline.org">http://suicidepreventionlifeline.org</a> <br>In a crisis, call their free and 24/ 7 U.S. hotline: 1-800-273-TALK (8255) <br>Contact their Crisis Text Line: text TALK to 741-741 <br>National Hopeline Network: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://hopeline.com">http://hopeline.com</a> / 1-800-442-HOPE (4673) <br>American Association of Suicidology: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://suicidology.org">http://suicidology.org</a> <br>American Foundation for Suicide Prevention: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://afsp.org">http://afsp.org</a> <br>Suicide Prevention Resource Center: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://sprc.org">http://sprc.org</a> <br><br>➽<b>FOR SUICIDE LOSS SURVIVORS:</b><br>Alliance of Hope for Suicide Survivors: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://allianceofhope.org">http://allianceofhope.org</a> <br>American Association of Suicidology survivors page: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://suicidology.org/suicide-survivors/suicide-loss-survivors">http://suicidology.org/suicide-surviv...</a> <br>Friends for Survival: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://friendsforsurvival.org">http://friendsforsurvival.org</a> <br>National Suicide Prevention Lifeline survivors page: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://suicidepreventionlifeline.org/help-yourself/loss-survivors/">http://suicidepreventionlifeline.org/...</a> <br>Suicide Awareness Voices of Education: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://save.org">http://save.org</a> <br><br>➽<b>UNDERSTANDING MENTAL ILLNESS:</b><br>Mental Health America: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mentalhealthamerica.net">http://mentalhealthamerica.net</a> <br>National Alliance on Mental Illness: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://nami.org">http://nami.org</a> <br>National Institute of Mental Health: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://nimh.nih.gov">http://nimh.nih.gov</a><br><br>Also, I found all of these resources from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2370725474" rel="nofollow noopener">The Astonishing Color of After by Emily X.R. Pan</a>, which is another amazing book that I completely recommend for anyone looking for more books that center around mental illness. And I’m obvious not a therapist, but my DMs will always be open for anyone who just needs a friend to talk to. You are deserving of love and happiness, sometimes it just takes a little while to find those things, but I promise you are worthy of them. And I promise that you matter. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCkQ3IFRLq4JSDt0OsFrtnTA" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexis</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily" rel="nofollow noopener">Lily</a>! ❤</span>

<div id="review_1746812549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1746812549" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1746812549?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=gay-mc">gay-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=books-that-made-me-cry">books-that-made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1746812549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9411930689256793353"><i>
  <blockquote> The universe may forget us but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on</blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/>When people used to say to me <i> what do you want to be when you grow up?</i> I'd <b>ALWAYS</b> say astronaut. In fact, I still <b>want</b> to be an astronaut .. I just don't think I will be ( unfortunately it turns out getting to space involves a shit ton of MATH and I don't do math very well.) <br/><br/>But the point stands I am absolutely a SLUT for space. What can I say, stars are pretty, planets intrigue me and I w</span>
  <span id="freeText9411930689256793353" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote> The universe may forget us but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on</blockquote>
</i> <br><br>When people used to say to me <i> what do you want to be when you grow up?</i> I'd <b>ALWAYS</b> say astronaut. In fact, I still <b>want</b> to be an astronaut .. I just don't think I will be ( unfortunately it turns out getting to space involves a shit ton of MATH and I don't do math very well.) <br><br>But the point stands I am absolutely a SLUT for space. What can I say, stars are pretty, planets intrigue me and I want to meet me some aliens (and yes aliens are real, you can't tell me in a universe of 60 tillion planets there aren't some aliens about somewhere) <br><br><b>ANYWAY</b>, this relates, I promise. <i>We are The Ants </i>has space, and aliens too. Space isn't the only thing that made me fall in love with this book but it helped. The aliens helped too. But what also helped was the incredible characters, the witty dialogue, the beautiful prose, the enchanting plot line, the emotions that this book dragged out of me and had churning within the first few pages. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478850744i/21120109._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478850745i/21120110._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><a href="http://dvnwild.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">by dvnwild on tumblr</a><br><br><br>Listen, I NEVER recommend contemporaries. <b> I DO NOT LIKE CONTEMPORARIES !!</b> Traditionally, anyway. Of course there was some that get me all emotional. We are the Ants is a contemporary I didn't just enjoy, but fell head over heels for. I love this book. <br><br><i>This book man</i>. It's kinda <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22628.The_Perks_of_Being_a_Wallflower" title="The Perks of Being a Wallflower by Stephen Chbosky" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perks of Being a Wallflower</a> meets <b>ET</b> and holy shit I love it. Our main character, Henry Denton, is a victim of reoccurring alien abductions. (YES PEOPLE, aliens are a thing in this book) and yet somehow the fact the aliens abduct him <i>all the time</i> (And at inconvenient times might I add) that isn't even his <b>main problem</b> Because not only do the aliens abduct him, they've also told him the world is ending in 144 days unless he stops it. <br><br>Actually, I wanna slow this down and sober it up a bit because it is a <b>heavy book.</b> And like, the space and aliens are fun but this book isn't entirely fun. Henry Denton, the protagonist, is coping with a lot. His dad walked out on his family, his mum is a mess, his unemployed college drop out brother has a pregnant girlfriend and Henry's boyfriend, Jesse, recently committed suicide. So on top of alien invasions he's dealing with a bit. He's supposed to save the world for the aliens, and he's not even sure it's worth it. <br><br>(<b>I KNOW THIS SEEMS ALOT OF INFO BUT IT'S NOT SPOILERS PROMISE</b> <br><br>This book is heavy, and it's bizarre and I <b>love it</b>. The main character is wonderful. I constantly have an issue with how teenage boys are written in books - I can never connect. But I connected with Henry, <i>oh my god</i> I loved him. I sympathised with him so much, <i>I understood him completely</i> and I found him to be a perceptive, thoughtful narrator who successfully gave me an existisitential crisis. And me, a catastrophic thinker, could relate a little too much to his overthinking. <br><br>But really, I love all the characters in this. Mysterious Diego, Audrey, Marcus and Zooey, I loved them all by the end. (but not Adrian tho. Fuck Adrian. ) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and especially fuck Marcus for the end.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The most beautiful thing about this though was the prose. The writing was <b>literally stunning</b>. Rich, with a wry tone and a frank perspective on the world. I enjoyed that while it was philosophical and reflective, it was also a bit deadpan and didn't beat around the bush. I liked the way this book offered a reflection on the things that worry us as people, and how it was ultimately hopeful despite all the despair and the heaviness of some of the themes. <br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478746286ra/21107641.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><br><br>We Are the Ants covers some heavy themes and topics. I loved it for it's LGBT+ representation, but be aware there are trigger warnings for <i>rape, suicide</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and miscarriage <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br>Despite that I think it's important, and I'm glad this book gave an honest perspective into some of the troubles facing both the teenage lgbt+ community, but also just teenagers in general. I loved the cast of diverse characters with interesting backstories. <b>AND I LOVED THE REPRESENTATION OF MEDICATION !! STOP DEMONISING MEDICATION IN YOUR BOOKS</b> But this book man. .. It can be dark, and heavy and it weighs on you, you truly feel the depth and weight of this book. I adore that. I adore it. <br><br>I loved the messages this book sent, and the way the problems and issues were tackled. I liked that things were not neatly tied in a bow, I liked the ambiguous ending. <br><br>In fact, there wasn't much at all I didn't like (it is a 5* book for a reason). But this is one of those books that was a 5* from the opening page to the last. There was simply not a moment I did not love? I read this in one sitting pretty much and I was emotionally drained by the end, but I was in love. <br><br>I've truly never read anything like this. For me, contemporary YA is becoming alot of the <b>same</b> but this stood out. I haven't been so shook by a contemporary since I read The Perks of Being a Wallflower back in 2012 or something. <br><br>I adore this book so much. I think everyone should read it. It's raw, it's honest. A poignant insight into people, and how we so desperately try to make things matter. A reminder that we matter on a small level to those around us, that being great does not mean achieving fame and notoriety. <br><br>And it's incredibly, disgustingly underrated and under read. This book is truly beautiful, and important and still makes me so emotional just by looking at the cover. I think about this book everyday. It deserves more attention, it's a truly beautiful book. <br><br>It's a book about remembering and cherishing the small things, about learning to let go, about loving fiercely and making sacrifices. About remembering we are who we are, that we define ourselves. That we matter. Oh, and it's about <i>aliens too. </i> <br><br><br><a href="https://play.spotify.com/user/jamieson_k/playlist/6V6oiYSB5B8uWNHiN40vEi" rel="nofollow noopener"> MY "WE ARE THE ANTS" PLAYLIST</a><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“We're not words, Henry, we're people.<br>Words are how others define us, but we can define ourselves any way we choose.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478850745ra/21120111.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9411930689256793353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522825668?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522825668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8513979654455981961"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455522418i/18111528._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is, my friends - <b>without any doubt - the most unexpected and remarkable book I've read this year (and the year before, if I'm being honest), soothing and yet poignant at the same time</b>. I feel as if I should wait and write a better review because let's face it, my midnight thoughts hardly come close to what this book deserves but I can't. I'm ecstatic and barely thinking straight as huge is its impact on me, and honestly? I need to vent.<br/><br/>As far as 5 stars ratings are concerned, mines are ofte</span>
  <span id="freeText8513979654455981961" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455522418i/18111528._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is, my friends - <b>without any doubt - the most unexpected and remarkable book I've read this year (and the year before, if I'm being honest), soothing and yet poignant at the same time</b>. I feel as if I should wait and write a better review because let's face it, my midnight thoughts hardly come close to what this book deserves but I can't. I'm ecstatic and barely thinking straight as huge is its impact on me, and honestly? I need to vent.<br><br>As far as 5 stars ratings are concerned, mines are often of two kinds : the flashy, mind-blowing, usually crazy ones (what? I love my evil cutters), and the quietly unforgettable others. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants" title="We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are the Ants</a> is part of the latter : <b>I can't, for the life of me, think about something I didn't like in this strange and beautiful story</b>. <br><br>Closing this novel, I feel like a walking-talking-contradiction : speechless, and yet so many words are fighting fiercely into my mind for the honor of - perhaps - convincing you to give it the chance I strongly think it deserves. <br><br>► Must I mention <b>the splendid characterization that gives life to these flawed, multi-layered and endearing human beings, whose relationships are pictured in such honest and real way?</b> Speaking of which, do you know why I think that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3130410.Shaun_David_Hutchinson" title="Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Shaun David Hutchinson</a> shows so much talent when creating his characters? Because albeit begrudgingly, I can't hate any member of Henry's family - they're messed-up sometimes, but oh, how they ring true! Their struggles, their reluctances, their mistakes - none of them can hide the profound love they feel for each others, even if they don't always know how to show that <i>yes</i>, they do care. Also, Diego. Gah. I won't say much and let you discover this hopeful wonder of a boy by yourself but trust me, he won't let you indifferent. <br><br>► Can I gush about the fact that <b>everything is beautifully crafted, every event way more complicated than it first appears?</b> Forget the blurb and your - well-deserved - doubts : although Henry's journey is freaking weird, it <i>works</i> wonderfully.<br><br>► Should I talk about the heartbreaking yet so realistic confusion between what the characters believe about themselves and the reality? <b>How the fog they're walking in can be both their end and their relief?</b> How Henry's narration, hovering between lucidity and delusion, never loses its hilarious and off-beat spikes, especially when he describes the world we're living in? Gosh, I'm still recovering from the SnowFlake Page. So fucking true. <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455534748i/18114119._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>☞ I could go on and on and <i>on</i> for hours, it wouldn't do it more justice than this little sentence can : <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants" title="We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are the Ants</a> is brilliant, and like nothing I read before. Oh, who am I kidding? It just entered my all-times favorites. Highly recommended</b>.<br><br><b>PS.</b> I may never get over the giant cockroaches. Bloody <i>HELL</i>. <br><br><b>Reread 06/25</b> : Granted, I have no time to come on Goodreads lately, let alone read. Yet I woke up this morning, took a look at the news and thought, THIS WORLD SUCKS. I know that it will seem incredibly arrogant, but I can't stand the general idiocy anymore. If there have always been subjects that maddened me (gender equality, racism, you name it), it seems to me that they keep multiply on a daily basis. Am I the only one who gets the impression that everything I care about is imploding? That we're stupidly taking a path that destroyed us in the past? Although I'm not sure that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23677341.We_Are_the_Ants" title="We Are the Ants by Shaun David Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are the Ants</a> will help, I need the break, really. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2082797306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2082797306" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2082797306?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=eh">eh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-and-a-half-stars">1-and-a-half-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2082797306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16585974434121230823">Bleh. <br/><br/>Like. I’m sure if you click with this book - if you care about the characters, if you believe the world, if you’re invested - it’s super meaningful and powerful and great.<br/><br/>But if you DON’T do those things…<br/><br/>it is truly a one-way plane ticket to sadness and suffering. And boy oh boy is it a turbulent ride.<br/><br/>No surprise, I’m of the latter group.<br/><br/>This is actually, legitimately 455 pages of horrifying bleakness. Imagine every terrible thing you can think of including in a young adult book, and there</span>
  <span id="freeText16585974434121230823" style="display:none">Bleh. <br /><br />Like. I’m sure if you click with this book - if you care about the characters, if you believe the world, if you’re invested - it’s super meaningful and powerful and great.<br /><br />But if you DON’T do those things…<br /><br />it is truly a one-way plane ticket to sadness and suffering. And boy oh boy is it a turbulent ride.<br /><br />No surprise, I’m of the latter group.<br /><br />This is actually, legitimately 455 pages of horrifying bleakness. Imagine every terrible thing you can think of including in a young adult book, and there’s an 8 in 10 chance you’ll find it in this manuscript of pain.<br /><br />Bullying? Yes.<br /><br />Suicidal thoughts? You betcha.<br /><br />Suicide? Uh huh.<br /><br />Depression? Nonstop, baby.<br /><br />Grief (over the death of a friend / boyfriend)? Forever.<br /><br />Abuse? All over the place.<br /><br />I’m not someone who judges a book by the number of trigger warnings it needs. To be honest, the pre-release discussion around <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3000833409?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ninth House</a> really pissed me off, because a book doesn’t need to be under a certain restriction for the number of difficult topics it’s allowed to include. And in Ninth House, everything that was included was included for a reason.<br /><br />That is not the case, in my opinion, for We Are the Ants.<br /><br />Here, it’s gratuitous.<br /><br />Not much happens in this book that isn’t completely difficult to read. There’s actually no plot other than the reader watching the protagonist suffer.<br /><br />I sincerely felt that everything was left by the wayside that wasn’t pain. Characters felt flat and undeveloped, the world (which included ALIENS!) was half-baked, the plot was nonexistent, and relationship and development arcs were completely thrown together at the end.<br /><br />In short, this was a massive bummer. And basically for no reason.<br /><br />Bottom line: Again, if this book worked for you and meant something to you, I’m not trying to take that away. But for me, it was nothing more than 455 pages of ouch ouch ouch.<br /><br />----------<br /><i>currently reading updates</i><br /><br />this book should have a "you must be this tall to read" sign.........<br /><br />...<br /><br />.....because it's an emotional rollercoaster. 😎</span>
  <a data-text-id="16585974434121230823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2400732090" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2400732090" />
    <a title="lily ☁️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10148904-lily"><img alt="lily ☁️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517405104p2/10148904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2400732090?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lily ☁️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lily ☁️" href="/user/show/10148904-lily">lily ☁️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25857011-we-are-the-ants">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=tolino">tolino</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=lgbtqiap-rep">lgbtqiap-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=prn-magic">prn-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=neurodiverse">neurodiverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2400732090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9484841083795857307">➳ <b>1 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/><b>“I finally finished this book, and I could cry tears of relief,”</b> was my first thought, after doing so. <i>We Are the Ants</i> had a few meaningful moments and one or two quotes that resonated with me, but all in all, too many things irritated me too much for me to rate this higher than 1 1/2 stars.<br/><br/>I spent about 85% (more than 400 pages!!) of this book wanting to give up on it, but since everyone loves it so much, I decided to finish it, and give it a fair chance to win me over as well. It </span>
  <span id="freeText9484841083795857307" style="display:none">➳ <b>1 1/2 stars</b><br /><br /><b>“I finally finished this book, and I could cry tears of relief,”</b> was my first thought, after doing so. <i>We Are the Ants</i> had a few meaningful moments and one or two quotes that resonated with me, but all in all, too many things irritated me too much for me to rate this higher than 1 1/2 stars.<br /><br />I spent about 85% (more than 400 pages!!) of this book wanting to give up on it, but since everyone loves it so much, I decided to finish it, and give it a fair chance to win me over as well. It didn’t.<br /><br /><i>We Are the Ants</i>’ story felt all over the place, as if it couldn’t decide on whether to be a contemporary with a paranormal twist, or a coming of age sci-fi story with a focus on a realistic, and real life character and relationship exploration. Not to use its acknowledgments against it, but I guess that’s what I’ll do, because it only serves to reinforce how I already feel about the book:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Every book is a challenge, but this one more than most. It began life as a haunted-house story, then became a murder mystery, then somehow morphed into a sci-fi story set on a space station before finally revealing its true self to me.”</i>
</blockquote><br />It tried to address so many sensitive subjects—bullying, suicide, depression, abuse, addiction, struggling to come to terms with your sexuality, and the meaning of life—that every single subject it addressed ended up feeling half-heartedly touched upon.<br /><br />I can <s>kind of</s> see why so many people love this book <s>if I squint really hard</s>, because it has a few quite touching scenes that were filled with relatively meaningful revelations—but all in all, the negatives more than outweighed the positives.<br /><br /><blockquote><b><u>What I Disliked</u>:</b> (This is the part in which I rant, read at your own risk.)<br /><br />- <b>The writing is incredibly dry</b> and doesn’t help much in drawing you into the story—rather the opposite. I came out of slump, just before I started this book, and it managed to nudge me back into one.<br />- <b>The “humor” is so overdone</b>, and I was tired of its attempts at being funny in a sarcastic way by the third joke.<br />- All the romances in this book were <b>tell rather than show</b>, and it gave them a very disingenuous feel.<br />- The same goes for <b>the portrayal of depression</b>. We are told that a character had/has depression, but it’s never really touched upon, or actually <i>noticeable</i>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Henry <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is supposedly depressed as well, but we never read about him actually being depressed, we’re only told that he is (unless I missed something during the times in which my eyes glazed over with apathy).<br />- Many of my favorite characters are anti-heroines who are flawed and don’t always behave in the most laudable ways, but <b>every single character is so <i>unlikable</i></b> here, which leads me to my next point:<br />- <b>All kinds of abuse are excused, justified, or simply accepted and forgiven</b>, without any sign that the responsible character feels any remorse or regret towards his or her actions.<br />- <b>The crudity</b>. I don’t know if it was Hutchinson’s attempt at making Henry sound more like a teenager, but I refuse to believe that teenage boys think about masturbation and male genitalia as often as Henry does, or draw references to those in the most non-sexual situations—it was ridiculous.<br /><br /><u><b>What I Liked</b></u>:<br /><br />+ Henry and Audrey’s friendship. It had a believable, and well-created arc, and Audrey is the only character (next to Diego … kind of) I actually took to.</blockquote><br /><b><u>To conclude</u>:</b> In the end, I feel like a huge weight had been lifted off my shoulders, when I finally flipped the page and landed on the one with the Acknowlegments—and I think that really says it all.<br /><br /><blockquote>☄️ <b>buddy</b> read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3030788-melanie" rel="nofollow noopener">Mel</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14852599-sofia-bookish-wanderess" rel="nofollow noopener">Sofia</a></blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/sprnklsofdreams" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sprinklesofdreamsx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://sprinklesofdreams.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/sprinkles-dreams-19449885" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13453148633537300848">the fact that i enjoyed a book about aliens makes me worried that i was abducted and brainwashed by aliens. lol. <br/><br/>in many ways, this reminded me of hutchinsons other book, <i>‘at the edge of the universe.’</i> they were different where it mattered, but the structure and overall basis of the books were quite similar. so much so that i could probably copy my review for ATEOTU and paste it here and it would work just fine. <br/><br/>again, hutchinson shows that he has a talent for writing heart-wrenching, but hopefu</span>
  <span id="freeText13453148633537300848" style="display:none">the fact that i enjoyed a book about aliens makes me worried that i was abducted and brainwashed by aliens. lol. <br /><br />in many ways, this reminded me of hutchinsons other book, <i>‘at the edge of the universe.’</i> they were different where it mattered, but the structure and overall basis of the books were quite similar. so much so that i could probably copy my review for ATEOTU and paste it here and it would work just fine. <br /><br />again, hutchinson shows that he has a talent for writing heart-wrenching, but hopeful, stories. he is able to tackle various sensitive topics (maybe even too many at times) but still have his story be realistic and genuine. but where he gets me is his writing. i dont annotate my books, but if i did, i think about 80% of my book would be highlighted. just the way he crafts his words to make them so raw and relatable is impressive. i especially love how he showed that science is present in every aspect of our lives, even explaining that its what makes life beautiful. <br /><br />this book resonated with me more than i thought it would and SDH keeps bumping himself up on my favourite authors list. i cant wait to read more from him!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2206931881?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206931881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13460529328712595630"><i>“Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe. But you don't. Because we are the ants.”</i><br/><br/>This is going to be slightly difficult to review. <br/>Our main character has been abducted by aliens. They give him a choice. A choice where the fate of the world rests on his shoulder. He's been given 144 days to decide whether he wants to end to world or save it. But Henry isn't sure whether he wants to. <br/><br/>Safe to say this is an important book, bec</span>
  <span id="freeText13460529328712595630" style="display:none"><i>“Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe. But you don't. Because we are the ants.”</i><br /><br />This is going to be slightly difficult to review. <br />Our main character has been abducted by aliens. They give him a choice. A choice where the fate of the world rests on his shoulder. He's been given 144 days to decide whether he wants to end to world or save it. But Henry isn't sure whether he wants to. <br /><br />Safe to say this is an important book, because of the numerous themes it discusses, the pivotal point being about life itself and how insignificant our impact on the world really is, since, really, <i>‘we are the ants.’</i> <br />I love how the author spoke about life through Henry's eyes and the casual alien abducting him. Despite that addition, it all felt too painfully real. <br />The tone of our main character was captured so well. As a reader, I felt his emotions, his despair, his constant questioning of his worth and identity and his battle with grief and depression. I was walking with him through his journey and desperately wanted things for him to get better!<br /><br />It was intense. The story was narrated in such a unique fashion, it racks with ones brains. It’s heavy, humorous, dark and slightly traumatic and puts forth the question: Is the world worth saving? Living? And if you had the power to stop the world from ending, would you?</span>

<div id="review_1454722058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454722058" />
    <a title="Gabby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby"><img alt="Gabby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482222518p2/26560207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1454722058?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabby" href="/user/show/26560207-gabby">Gabby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=amazing-ending">amazing-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=books-to-reread-in-the-future">books-to-reread-in-the-future</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=incredible-plot-twists">incredible-plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26560207-gabby?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454722058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6688989408496649523">I just reread this book for the third time and it was absolutely incredible again. <br/><b>
  <blockquote>"Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe. But you don't. Because we are the ants."</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Holy shit you guys, this book just changed my life I think. This book just reminded me why I love reading and why I read books. I don't even know how to properly review this incredible book. the premise of this story sounds ridiculous - a teenage boy Henry is</span>
  <span id="freeText6688989408496649523" style="display:none">I just reread this book for the third time and it was absolutely incredible again. <br><b>
  <blockquote>"Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe. But you don't. Because we are the ants."</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Holy shit you guys, this book just changed my life I think. This book just reminded me why I love reading and why I read books. I don't even know how to properly review this incredible book. the premise of this story sounds ridiculous - a teenage boy Henry is abducted by aliens and the aliens tell him the world is coming to an end, but he has the chance to prevent it by pressing this red button. But Henry struggles to decide whether or not the world is worth saving. Henry's life is hell; his boyfriend Jesse committed suicide, his Father left his family when he was 13, his older brother is an asshole to him most of the time and he just knocked up his girlfriend, and his grandma has dementia and doesn't always remember who they are. The premise of this story might sound ridiculous, but it was executed <b>so well.</b> <br><br><b>This is one of the most inspiring stories I've ever read.</b> As soon as I read the first chapter of this book I knew I would rate it 5 stars. The first chapter of this book is one of the most powerful and promising first chapters I've ever read. I picked up this book last night just wanting to start it, but I wasn't expecting to fall in love with it so quickly and devour this book the way I did. Last night I read 320 pages and this morning I woke up and went to the book store and purchased it so I could read the rest and highlight and tab and write in it. I think I used all of my blue tabs tabbing this book and my highlighter is almost out of ink. The way I can best describe this book would be: <b>Donnie Darko</b> meets <b>Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe</b> meets <b>The Perks of Being A Wallflower</b>. If you love any of these three things, you will fall in love with this story. I pictured Henry as Donnie Darko while I was reading because he fits the description perfectly, and like Donnie Darko, Henry thinks about the world ending and what he needs to do about it. This book is like Donnie Darko if Donnie Darko had GLBT and aliens.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455257468ra/18078835.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"That's the problem with memories: you can visit them, but you can't live in them."</b><br><br>Henry is very depressed, and some parts of this book were very hard to read. It made me cry more than once, quite often actually, and I really wanted to give him a hug. From the moment Diego was introduced in this book I knew I loved him. He's so positive and happy and he's such a good influence on Henry. Henry needs that in his life. Diego never judges him or questions him and he tells him things like: <b>"There's an amazing world out there for you to discover, Henry Denton, but you have to be willing to discover yourself first."</b> and just beautiful things like that. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I loved the way Diego talked about his family and what he did to protect people. It only made me love his character more when he said he finally hit their dad who had been beating his mom and sister for years, and that's why he went to juvenile detention for 2 years. Diego may be a hot head with an anger problem but he protects the people he loves and that says a lot. I also loved when Diego finally beat up Marcus at the end, after Marcus attempted to rape Henry. Diego went after him and broke his nose, and I love that Diego is so protective of Henry. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>"Dreams are hopeful because they exist as pure possibility. Unlike memories, which are fossils, long dead and buried deep."</b><br><br>This book is full of amazing, fleshed out characters. Everyone in this book has a story of their own, and experiences some kind of grief. His Mom, his brother Charley, Zoey (his brothers girlfriend), Diego, his teacher Ms. Faraci, Jesse's Mom, Marcus, Audrey (his best friend before Jesse died), Henry's grandmother who is slowly losing her memory. Everyone in this story makes an impact on Henry's life and has an incredibly detailed story of their own and I admire that. Also, this book is full of tragedy's and sometimes I even questioned whether the world (or at least Henry's world) was worth saving. I love how Henry would ask every single person he came into contact with if the world was coming to an end and they had the power to save it would they? And each character would give him a very unique and different response based on their situations and what they were going through. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[These sad tragedy's include: Henry getting beaten up in the showers by three guys in alien masks, and they dumped green paint all over him and called him Space Boy. Also when Marcus keeps tormenting him and humiliating him, and then at the end of the book he actually attempts to rape him. I wanted to cry for Henry several times and sometimes I did. Also, when Charley and Zoey lost their baby and delivered a still born, and seeing Charley lose his shit, it was so depressing. You could tell he really wanted to be a Father. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I loved the inspiring conversations Henry would have with Zooey and his Mother. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I loved when Henry was telling Zooey that Charley would make a terrible Father, and she went on to explain how he was the one who wanted to keep it and talked her out of an abortion. I think it showed Henry a different side to his brother and allowed him and Zooey to get closer. I also love how Henry encouraged his Mother to quit her waitress job and do what she wanted, to be a cook. He told her how she's so amazing and talented and if she would only get a mirror she would see it too. Then she finally quit her job and got hired as a chef, and Zooey asked what made her want to do it, and she said "Someone gave me a mirror", it was such a beautiful moment and I wanted to cry. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b>"Because you can only die once but you can suffer forever."</b><br><br>This book talks about life in the most honest and beautiful way in my opinion. It really makes you question why we do the things we do and whether it's all worth it. What do we do it all for? He constantly explains how the universe won't remember us and even when we die everything will carry on eventually. We're all going to die one way or another and we probably won' be remembered long after we die. It's just the reality, and I this book really dives deep into this idea of why we even bother living and doing the things we do. <b>"We remember the past, live in the present, and write the future."</b><br><br>This book blew me away honestly. I genuinely wasn't expecting to like it as much as I did. The first and last chapters of this book are some of the best first and last chapters in a book I've ever read. The last page of this book left me breathless and lost in thought. I'm in love with this story, with these characters. I don't remember the last time a book has affected me so emotionally like this one has. I think it's incredible when a book has the power to change a person, and in some small way, I really do believe this book has changed me. This story will stick with me for a very long time and I'm already looking forward to re-reading it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>The ending of this book reminded me of the ending of We All Looked Up. We never find out if the world ends or if Henry is just delusional and it was never real, but as Henry says at the end of this book, it doesn't really matter. At the end of the day, that isn't what this story was about. This story is about a teenage boy who is depressed and suicidal but through a series of tragic events, he discovers the meaning of life. I think the ending of this book is absolutely perfect and it gave me goosebumps and I feel really inspired. <br><br><b>"We may not get to choose how we die, but we can chose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on."</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455257777ra/18078861.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Book Playlist:</b><br>-Blood by The Middle East<br>-1904 by Benjamin Francis Leftwich<br>-Cycling Trivialities by Jose Gonzalez<br>-The Breach by Dustin Tebbutt<br>-Naked As We Came by Iron &amp; Wine<br>-Down The Line by Jose Gonzalez<br><br><b>First read: February 11th, 2016<br>Second read: October 12th, 2016 (audiobook)<br>Third read: December 26th, 2019</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
