<div id="review_2372394381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372394381" />
    <a title="Kayla Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70522717-kayla-dawn"><img alt="Kayla Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582845179p2/70522717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372394381?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla Dawn" href="/user/show/70522717-kayla-dawn">Kayla Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481475204" href="/book/show/27220730-we-are-the-ants">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372394381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4166230922690754248">Hmm. I don't really know tbh. This one is hard to rate for me. <br/><br/>First of all, this was a really quick read. I flew through the pages. The writing style was okay most of the time (But next time dear Hutchinson please double check if your translations are correct!! If you want to write something in a different language you need to make sure that it's not complete bullshit lol - he literally translated "I miss you so much Dad" with "Ich hab dich so sehr, Papa verpasst" - sorry for the english speaki</span>
  <span id="freeText4166230922690754248" style="display:none">Hmm. I don't really know tbh. This one is hard to rate for me. <br /><br />First of all, this was a really quick read. I flew through the pages. The writing style was okay most of the time (But next time dear Hutchinson please double check if your translations are correct!! If you want to write something in a different language you need to make sure that it's not complete bullshit lol - he literally translated "I miss you so much Dad" with "Ich hab dich so sehr, Papa verpasst" - sorry for the english speaking people but the germans will know why this is a blood bath) <br /><br />The dialogues felt real and it was easy to understand the emotions of the characters. I think Hutchinson portrayed a realistic way of grieving and blaming yourself, feeling guilty especially when you fall in love with someone else. <br /><br />I really "enjoyed" (weird in this context but you know) the storyline between Charlie and Zooey. Only time I cried while reading this book was because of something that happened to them. <br />Even though Charlie was a little overdone as a character particularly in his role as a brother. Pissing on Henrys homework because he didn't leave the bath quickly enough? Ok sure. <br /><br />I loved Audrey, she always tried to be a good friend and stood up against people who acted like assholes (except this one time where she said suicide is egoistic, please don't do that). <br /><br />Plus I absolutely adored the fact that Henry being homosexual wasn't a big deal at all. Don't get me wrong I love how this topics becomes more and more important and talked about but I also love seeing it as a normal part of our life, without being the point of attention. Because that's how it should be. Normal. <br /><br /><br /><br />But, <br /><br />I hated Henry. Seriously. He was awful 90% of time and treated everyone around him like shit. And he was always like "nothing matters, I don't matter" on the one hand but "it all is my fault, he did this because of me and he did that because of me" on the other hand which doesn't make much sense. <br />I get it, he was grieving and confused and didn't know how to feel but it bothers me so much that people in ya books about grieve always act like the feelings of other people don't matter. They always treat them like shit. That's just not okay. There are definitely people out there who act like that after losing someone but that doesn't make it any better. <br /><br />I also felt like the end was overdramatized. Thrown in just to make it a little more shocking I guess. I don't know it just felt a little unrealistic to me. <br /><br />I'm still not sure if this whole alien thing was supposed to be a metaphor or not. It's probably up to the reader to decide. I'd definitely prefer it if it was in his imagination only. Like sleepwalking or something tbh because it was just too crazy in an otherwise normal contemporary book in my opinion. <br /><br />Overall this was a good book, it makes you think. I'd definitely recommend it if you like this kind of contemporary books! ☺️<br /><br /><br />Review is a little all over the place because new thoughts always come to my mind and I have to throw them in somewhere lol sorry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4166230922690754248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer1620067577748038898">Update... from the book festival...<br/>Shaun David Hutchinson read the first two pages of his book.. a room of about 50 people were laughing hysterically. <br/>He is so real...<br/>So wonderful. He says he has ADHD. He was an average kid in school. One of the themes in is books is that his main character is average who is presented with extraordinary things to do. He wants to give the nerds a place to shine in the world. <br/><br/>His book "We Are The Ants" is really great!!!<br/>So is this author!!!!<br/><br/>"Popularity is teenage </span>
  <span id="freeText1620067577748038898" style="display:none">Update... from the book festival...<br />Shaun David Hutchinson read the first two pages of his book.. a room of about 50 people were laughing hysterically. <br />He is so real...<br />So wonderful. He says he has ADHD. He was an average kid in school. One of the themes in is books is that his main character is average who is presented with extraordinary things to do. He wants to give the nerds a place to shine in the world. <br /><br />His book "We Are The Ants" is really great!!!<br />So is this author!!!!<br /><br />"Popularity is teenage heroin. Kids who have tasted it crave more; those who have it in <br />abundance are revered as gods; and even those who have never basked in the light of glory secretly desire it, regardless of what they say to the contrary. Popularity can transform an otherwise normal kid into a narcissistic, ego-obsessed, materialistic asshole". <br />"Not that I would know. I have never been, nor wanted to be, popular. Popularity is the reason Marcus ridicules me in public and makes out with me when we're alone". <br />OUCH!!!!!!! That last sentence put such a wrench in my gut - I had a hard time letting it go. <br /><br />Henry Denton is dealing with grief.....(his boyfriend has committed suicide, he has loss friends, his father left their family, his grandmother has Alzheimer's--( she lives with them), his older brother Charlie punches him out if he feels like it, and is a college drop out who knocked up his girlfriend, Zooey. His mother is a chain smoker, and is struggling to hold his family together. <br />Oh....and aliens ( who abducted him at age 13 and have continued to take him from his bed to board their ship on and off for years)....has given him an "opportunity". <br />The world is going to end unless Henry pushes a big RED BUTTON. He has total responsibility whether or not to save the world. He is give 144 days to make up his mind. <br /><br />However, no matter what more I say about this book...no matter how many reviews you read... I swear to God.... unless you read it yourself ....word for word....<br />we might as well just talk about Cowboys and Indians. <br /><br />It's a book worth reading. You'll form strong opinions about the characters...( positive and negative). It's the type of story which could be read several time... as the layers are endless. <br /><br />For me...this book is less about being gay -( but Henry is gay), or coming of age - ( but he is still very young), but more about how we deal with grief - at any age! <br /><br />Brilliantly written ......( sci-fi....'soft')....for those who shy away from anything science fiction. A book to love and adore!<br /><br />*I get to meet the author Shaun David Hutchinson this coming weekend. I'm excited to hear him speak about this book!</span>

<div id="review_1623981314" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623981314" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623981314?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623981314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2641561481720636123">This book deserved more than 5 stars.<br/><br/>I stayed up until nearly 2:00 a.m. to finish this book and I cannot stop thinking about it. Honestly, I read a good amount of YA fiction, and a lot of it is tremendously well-written and emotionally evocative, but I've not been this blown away by a book since I read Jandy Nelson's <b>
  <i>I'll Give You the Sun</i>
</b>, which made <a href='http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2015/01/my-favorite-books-of-2014.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>my list of the best books I read in 2014</a>. <br/><br/>Seriously. This one was brutal and absolutely beautiful.<br/><br/>"Sometimes I think gravity may be death in di</span>
  <span id="freeText2641561481720636123" style="display:none">This book deserved more than 5 stars.<br /><br />I stayed up until nearly 2:00 a.m. to finish this book and I cannot stop thinking about it. Honestly, I read a good amount of YA fiction, and a lot of it is tremendously well-written and emotionally evocative, but I've not been this blown away by a book since I read Jandy Nelson's <b>
  <i>I'll Give You the Sun</i>
</b>, which made <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2015/01/my-favorite-books-of-2014.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">my list of the best books I read in 2014</a>. <br /><br />Seriously. This one was brutal and absolutely beautiful.<br /><br />"Sometimes I think gravity may be death in disguise. Other times I think gravity is love, which is why love's only demand is that we fall."<br /><br />For the last few years, aliens have periodically abducted Henry Denton. As if high school wasn't already difficult to deal with. The aliens don't tell Henry what they want from him or why they've chosen him, but apart from leaving him nearly naked in strange places all over his Florida town, they haven't hurt him too badly.<br /><br />No one believes Henry's stories, except his boyfriend Jesse. But Jesse recently killed himself, and Henry believes he is to blame, or at least should have seen how badly Jesse was hurting. Everyone else in Henry's life, including his fellow classmates, taunt him and call him "Space Boy," making every day at school a living hell. And his home life isn't much better—his mother works more and more shifts as a waitress while her real dream is to be a chef; his older brother abuses him physically and psychologically nearly every day; and his grandmother, suffering from Alzheimer's, seems to have fewer and fewer lucid moments.<br /><br />The aliens have given Henry an ultimatum: Earth will be destroyed in 144 days, unless Henry makes the decision to save the world. All he has to do is push a button. But does Henry <i>want</i> to save the world? Is the world really worth saving without Jesse in it? <br /><br />"Most people probably believe they would have pressed the button in my situation—nobody wants the world to end, right?—but the truth is that nothing is as simple as it seems. Turn on the news; read some blogs. The world is a shit hole, and I have to consider whether it might be better to wipe the slate clean and give the civilization that evolves from the ashes of our bones a chance to get it right."<br /><br />As the deadline draws closer, Henry searches for evidence that the world is worth saving—in the bully who wants to be with Henry in secret but terrorizes him in public; in Audrey, his former best friend, who used to be an enormous part of his life; in the new student who adds some mystery into Henry's life; and Henry's family members, each dealing with their own struggles. Sure, there are moments when life isn't so bad, but Henry has to decide whether humanity is worth saving or if letting the world end would also end his own emotional anguish.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>We Are the Ants</i>
</b> is a difficult book to read at times, emotionally. It seems incredible that Henry would allow himself to be treated the way he is by so many people, and that no one would put a stop to it, but the truth is, this type of thing happens more often than not in real life. He is such an incredible character—as are many of the supporting characters—that you root for them to be happy even as you begin to understand that maybe Henry's pain is too much for anyone to bear.<br /><br />That's not to say that the book is a total downer. There were many moments that made me smile and laugh, and moments that touched my heart and made me even cry good tears (as opposed to the ugly ones I cried at other times). I haven't ever read anything that Shaun David Hutchinson has written before, but after this, rest assured I will. This is such an inventive, moving, beautiful book I feel utterly privileged to have read. I won't soon forget it.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2641561481720636123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=speculative-lit-not-quite-sci-fi">speculative-lit-not-quite-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1807986751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9842000019208929950"><b> 4 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“We're not words, Henry, we're people. Words are how others define us, but we can define ourselves any way we choose.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Dude, that ending messed me <i>up.</i><br/><br/>Our story revolves around Henry, a teenager with what can only be described as a <i>shitty</i> home life.<br/><br/>So when Henry is given the option of letting the world end, or saving it at the press of a button-- he hesitates. <br/><br/>And the rest of what follows was a glorious expedition of character development, philosophy and profoundly unsettling question</span>
  <span id="freeText9842000019208929950" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“We're not words, Henry, we're people. Words are how others define us, but we can define ourselves any way we choose.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Dude, that ending messed me <i>up.</i><br /><br />Our story revolves around Henry, a teenager with what can only be described as a <i>shitty</i> home life.<br /><br />So when Henry is given the option of letting the world end, or saving it at the press of a button-- he hesitates. <br /><br />And the rest of what follows was a glorious expedition of character development, philosophy and profoundly unsettling questions. <br /><br /><b>Every character was purposeful.</b> Everyone was developed. <i>Every. One.</i> Henry’s jerktastic brother, Charlie. Their grandmother. Charlie’s pregnant girlfriend, Zooey. The school bully, Marcus. Audrey. Deigo. All of the character’s were allowed faults and insecurities, in addition to their personality quirks. They all feel <i>real.</i><br /><br />The plot tries to take a look at some harsh realities and <b>holds no punches.</b> There are some really heavy, painful subjects addressed, including: depression, suicide, abuse and homophobia. All this weight had the potential to sink the story, but it’s handled in nuanced ways framed by the complicated characters. Instead, the plot goes along with Henry’s nihilistic and confused outlook, further complicating the moral dilemma. <br /><br />I also appreciated how <b>this isn’t a case of love-fixes-everything.</b> Diego is an important part of the plot, and a developed character, but meeting him isn’t necessarily what fundamentally changes Henry’s world, like the blurb suggests. Instead, Henry has to determine his own world-view and make his own decision about the save-the-world-button. <br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this and thought it was expertly crafted. I had a few problems with some pacing, and certain points I felt a little redundant-- <i>just</i> teetering this side of melodrama. But this is a really special story, and I don’t know I’ve ever read anything like it. <br /><br />Failed BR with the always lovely, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/56485897-alyssa" rel="nofollow noopener">Alyssa!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9842000019208929950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1853956504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1343872196281572600">4 to 4.5 stars<br/><br/>While many of the elements of this book are recognizable as common to recent YA novels, there are several unique elements that make this book stand out as different. Overall, a very enthralling book.<br/><br/>Here are some of my thoughts.<br/><br/>- Lots of great and interesting characters. For me, all the people we meet in this story each play a big part in bringing it all together. Also, everyone you meet takes a huge journey from page 1 to page 451<br/>- Maybe a bit heavy on the cynical melodrama; lots </span>
  <span id="freeText1343872196281572600" style="display:none">4 to 4.5 stars<br /><br />While many of the elements of this book are recognizable as common to recent YA novels, there are several unique elements that make this book stand out as different. Overall, a very enthralling book.<br /><br />Here are some of my thoughts.<br /><br />- Lots of great and interesting characters. For me, all the people we meet in this story each play a big part in bringing it all together. Also, everyone you meet takes a huge journey from page 1 to page 451<br />- Maybe a bit heavy on the cynical melodrama; lots of woe-is-me moments. At points it becomes exhausting. However, I think it does end up lending well to the development of the characters and the story (if it doesn't bother you too much on the way).<br />- Very gritty and real. Now, I am not sure it is realistic, per se, but the events of the story are real and raw. Sometimes books get right to the edge of taking a chance, but don't cross that line, but this book jumps feet first into topics like sexuality, depression, suicide, rape, and others that might be too spoiler-ish to mention.<br /><br />It was quite a ride and definitely worth reading. It might be too much for some since it does get quite intense. But, if you can and do read it, I think you will find it to be a satisfying and moving experience.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3073479835652353666">Henry Denton, a troubled teenage boy, has been abducted by aliens. More precisely, he's been abducted by the same group of aliens multiple times over the span of many years.<br/><br/>But now, things have changed. The aliens have recently given Henry a choice.   <b>OR</b>

  <span id="freeText3073479835652353666" style="display:none">Henry Denton, a troubled teenage boy, has been abducted by aliens. More precisely, he's been abducted by the same group of aliens multiple times over the span of many years.<br /><br />But now, things have changed. The aliens have recently given Henry a choice. He can choose to save the world, <i>
  <b>OR</b>
</i> he can watch it all end in just a mere 144 days.<br /><br />What??!! OH. MY. GOD.<br /><br />Needless to say, it's a <i>massive</i> responsibility to put on the shoulders of just one high school boy. Is the world even worth saving? Should he just end it all now and save everyone from their misery?<br /><br /><i>WELL...</i> as I suspected in the beginning, this story is <i>actually</i> about something else. The good news is this was a heartfelt, emotional story with well-developed characters and a great ending.<br /><br />I just felt misled because this was marketed as a sci-fi book, and it just so happens I was very much in the mood for an engrossing sci-fi read. I simply wasn't expecting what I got. Ah well. I think I'm going to promptly head over to the sci-fi section. 😏</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14051060874705472825">This book is so <i>special</i>. At some parts it seems like every other YA contemporary, but then at some parts it's just <b>so much more.</b> Its touching, deep and really makes you <i>feel</i>. I'm so glad I didn't DNF this, which I was very close to doing. <br/><br/>What I loved the most about this book, is that <b>it leaves you thinking and questioning your life.   <span id="freeText14051060874705472825" style="display:none">This book is so <i>special</i>. At some parts it seems like every other YA contemporary, but then at some parts it's just <b>so much more.</b> Its touching, deep and really makes you <i>feel</i>. I'm so glad I didn't DNF this, which I was very close to doing. <br /><br />What I loved the most about this book, is that <b>it leaves you thinking and questioning your life. It leaves a mark on you.</b> <br /><br />This book is about a boy named Henry. <br />His life is very fucked up. <br />His boyfriend commit suicide. <br />His brother is a college dropout who got his girlfriend pregnant.<br />His dad left him when he was young. <br />His mom smokes and is trying to keep their broken family together. <br />He gets bullied, verbally and physically in school. <br />He is losing his grandmother to Alheizmer's.<br />Henry needs to act like he's okay, but he's not.<br />Aliens have abducted Henry and given him the choice to press a button in order to save the world. If he doesn't the world will end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Obviously, it's all in his head, right? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If I were Henry, experiencing what he is going through, I sure as fuck, wouldn't believe the world is worth saving. That's one of the things I loved most about this book, <b>being able to relate to Henry so much.</b> He is such a <b>realistic</b> character and you <b>feel</b> what he goes through, you <b>understand</b> what he goes through. <br /><br />I loved reading this book, however, about 40% of this bored me to death and just seemed like every other contemporary. What really stopped me from giving this below 3 stars was the ending. It was worth it and just plain beautiful. <br />◇<br /><br />◇<br /><br />◇<br />BR with my fellow <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/34598553-alaska-myers" rel="nofollow noopener">Wolf lover.</a> <s>who I have betrayed, read ahead and finished.</s></span>

<div id="review_3535937073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3535937073" />
    <a title=" jd 지훈" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67798563-jd"><img alt=" jd 지훈" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598751562p2/67798563.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3535937073?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" jd 지훈" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" jd 지훈" href="/user/show/67798563-jd"> jd 지훈</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67798563-jd?shelf=rave">rave</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67798563-jd?shelf=supercalifragilisticexpialidocious">supercalifragilisticexpialidocious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3535937073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer483654521811303275">Note: Content and trigger warnings are written at the end as they may contain spoilers.<br/><br/><i>"We may not get to choose how we die, but we can choose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn’t matter. Because we are the ants, and we’ll keep marching on."</i><br/><br/><b>Calypso, Florida (2015–2016)</b> — The world will end in 144 days. At least, that's what <i>Henry Denton</i> knows based on the ultimatum he was given by the aliens who periodically abduct him. But Henry can prevent this by simply pressing a big red b</span>
  <span id="freeText483654521811303275" style="display:none">Note: Content and trigger warnings are written at the end as they may contain spoilers.<br /><br /><i>"We may not get to choose how we die, but we can choose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn’t matter. Because we are the ants, and we’ll keep marching on."</i><br /><br /><b>Calypso, Florida (2015–2016)</b> — The world will end in 144 days. At least, that's what <i>Henry Denton</i> knows based on the ultimatum he was given by the aliens who periodically abduct him. But Henry can prevent this by simply pressing a big red button, only he wasn't sure himself if he wants to, especially if life hasn't really been kind to him. After all, aren't we all just insignificant specks of dust in the universe? We believe that we matter but we really don't—because in reality, we are only so little: for <b>We Are the Ants</b>.<br /><br /><b>IF THE WORLD IS GONNA END IN 144 DAYS, SHOULD YOU READ THIS BOOK? Man, you definitely fucking should.</b><br /><br />So when I saw that my Goodreads and Booktube gods <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1503480390?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily May</a>¹, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430253248?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kai</a>², <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026464143?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily Fox</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454722058?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Gabby</a>³, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618386946?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lala</a> all rated this five stars, I told myself that I had to fucking read this book as soon as possible. Thank the universe that I did because this novel did what? <i>THAT</i>, my friends. It did that.<br /><br /><b>Damn, I just can't believe it was so fucking good.</b> <i>What the hell?</i> Am I on earth? The last time I checked, things this good don't exist nor happen here.<br /><br />Before picking this up, I was actually having a blame game with myself on my inability to finish reading a book as soon as I can, and I was ready to settle with the fact that the blame lies on me until this book slapped me with a big <b>no</b>. <i>"You just need a perfect book to spend your precious time for," Ants whispered on my ear as a gentle reminder.</i><br /><br />This book was so compelling that even just by thinking of it, I wanted to continue immersing myself on Henry's world (even if my schedule is <i>that</i> packed because university is being a bitch, as usual). Don't get me wrong, I still love university. Stay in school, kids. Please don't mind my love-hate relationship with university. It be like that sometimes. Lol.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Out in the world, crawling in a field at the edge of some bullshit town with a name like Shoshoni or Medicine Bow, is an ant. You weren’t aware of it. Didn’t know whether it was a soldier, a drone, or the queen. Didn’t care if it was scouting for food to drag back to the nest or building new tunnels for wriggly ant larvae. Until now that ant simply didn’t exist for you. If I hadn’t mentioned it, you would have continued on with your life, pinballing from one tedious task to the next—shoving your tongue into the bacterial minefield of your girlfriend’s mouth, doodling the variations of your combined names on the cover of your notebook—waiting for electronic bits to zoom through the air and tell you that someone was thinking about you. That for one fleeting moment you were the most significant person in someone else’s insignificant life. But whether you knew about it or not, that ant is still out there doing ant things while you wait for the next text message to prove that out of the seven billion self-centered people on this planet, you are important. Your entire sense of self-worth is predicated upon your belief that you matter, that you matter to the universe.<br /><br />But you don’t.<br /><br />Because we are the ants.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />On a serious note, <b>the level of depth that Hutchinson managed to portray his characters with is immensely astounding.</b> As someone who really appreciates complex, round, and dynamic characters, the characterization and character development in this book earned <i>Ants</i> a special place in my heart's favorites shelf. I can only think of a handful of books whose characters are this raw and intricate, and that shows how exceptional this one is. Don't even get me started with me pitying a bully in some instances because I being masochistic like that is a big no-no. Lmao. <i>But that's how effective the narrative is as he was shown as an actual person who is fucked-up yet still authentic.</i><br /><br /><b>The layers of the prose? The complexities of the narrative? The interweaving of the characters' relationships and histories? Just beautiful. Tan hermoso. Napakaganda. 너무 아름다워요.</b><br /><br />The use of language though. I'm gobsmacked. <i>Bloody hell.</i> Hutchinson's writing style is evocatively poignant yet geekly enigmatic at the same time. As far as my preferences go, this is the perfect balance of the kind of prose I want to read in a YA novel. <b>Smart yet vulnerable. Humanely warm yet mysteriously cold.</b><br /><br />However, I personally think that the main protagonist is the most significant factor why this book is either a hit or miss for the readers. You'll either love him or hate him. Luckily, I related to Henry so much because he is basically my young edgy, witty, and nihilist self which Hutchinson masterfully constructed in this book, making me feel genuinely represented. I may not have undergone all the sad, horrendous things that happened to him but at their core, those events share similarities on my personal history.<br /><br />Moreover, I never thought that a book can be an accurate representation of the intersection of my two greatest worlds: science and philosophy. This makes the space geek in me squeal and the ever-wandering philosopher in my soul finally have his long-overdue eureka moment.<br /><br />On a darker note though, this novel hits home on the trauma people have when a loved one dies of suicide alongside the grief that comes with it. As someone who has had suicidal thoughts myself, this book became a great reminder on how my family and my close friends will suffer the moment I stopped meditating, taking care of myself, and listening to my psychiatrist and psychologist—ending up just wallowing to what my mental issues want me to do. It was a hard pill to swallow, but I'd do it for a narrative this poignant and important. <br /><br />Oftentimes, subjects like these fall into the wrong hands, and such authors make a whole wreckage out of the sensitive issues that need to be discussed with utmost care. There are writers who use angst for angst's sake and include mental illnesses on their narratives but irresponsibly handle them. But I stand here proudly to flex my boy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3130410.Shaun_David_Hutchinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Shaun David Hutchinson</a> for proving that he isn't like any of those authors.<br /><br /><b>Also, can we talk about how therapy and proper medical assistance were highlighted as essential for the recovery on mental health issues?</b> It means so much to me as someone who was saved and was taken care of by my psychiatrist and therapist. (<i>All The...</i> *coughs* <i>Bright...</i> *coughs* can't relate.) <br /><br />We are blessed that Hutchinson's talent and wisdom gave these topics justice as they were handled with acute cognizance and sensitivity. This makes this novel and Hutchinson himself really special to me. <b>I just love this book to death.</b> <br /><br />Now I can safely say that <i>Ants</i> sits there with <i>Aristotle and Dante</i> and <i>I'll Give You The Sun</i> as my gay contemporary holy trinity.<br /><br />Rep: LGBTQ+ | mental health awareness, equality, acceptance<br /><br />P.S. Read this while listening to Alec Benjamin, Conan Gray, Keshi, Ruel, and Troye Sivan and you're there for an atmospheric sentimental ride. (Not my music taste revealing how much of a fuck boy I am. Please don't trust me. Lmao.)🤙<br /><br /><b>Personal Enjoyment:</b> 5 stars<br /><b>Quality of the Book:</b> 4.9 stars<br />- Use of Language: ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br />- Plot and Narrative Arc: ⭐⭐⭐⭐+<br />- Characters: ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br />- Integrity: ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br />- Message: ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br /><br />AVG: <b>4.95 stars</b><br /><br />- - -<br />Notes:<br />[1] Emily May's insights on the characters and the prose of the novel are worth reading.<br />[2] Kai's analysis on the subtle messages on the book re: Feminism and Sexuality is on-point and I couldn't agree more.<br />[3] Gabby's <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HmIm_b1dGFs" rel="nofollow noopener">book talk</a> about the novel made my heart full.<br /><br />- - -<br />CW/TW: trauma, grief, mentions of suicide, depression, suicidal ideation, homophobia, bullying, physical violence, sexual violence, assault, abuse, miscarriage/stillbirth<br /><br />- - -<br />Status Updates:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313701244" rel="nofollow noopener">시작</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313710482" rel="nofollow noopener">9월30일 (1)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313726152" rel="nofollow noopener">9월30일 (2)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313736227" rel="nofollow noopener">9월30일 (3)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313811112" rel="nofollow noopener">10월1일 (1)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313855207" rel="nofollow noopener">10월1일 (2)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313871698" rel="nofollow noopener">10월1일 (3)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313880761" rel="nofollow noopener">10월1일 (4)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313889237" rel="nofollow noopener">10월1일 (5)</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/313898667" rel="nofollow noopener">끝</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2909463008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2909463008" />
    <a title="Sandeep" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/96868145-sandeep"><img alt="Sandeep" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563973462p2/96868145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2909463008?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandeep" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandeep" href="/user/show/96868145-sandeep">Sandeep</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/96868145-sandeep?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2909463008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13712464183849443979"><i>
  <b>" We may not get to choose how we die, but we can chose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on."</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/>The premise of this book is so misleading - A teenage boy is abducted by aliens and they tell him the world is going to end, but they give him a choice to prevent it by pushing a button. Sounds ridiculous, right? But there is so much more to this book than that, it is not even the central theme of this book. It's a story </span>
  <span id="freeText13712464183849443979" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>" We may not get to choose how we die, but we can chose how we live. The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on."</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />The premise of this book is so misleading - A teenage boy is abducted by aliens and they tell him the world is going to end, but they give him a choice to prevent it by pushing a button. Sounds ridiculous, right? But there is so much more to this book than that, it is not even the central theme of this book. It's a story about discovering your own self, sexuality, parenthood, friendship, family and the ultimate question of 'Is life even worth living?' Honestly, I'm so overwhelmed by this book that I don't even think I can even review this properly. I'm gonna try though.<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>" Dreams are hopeful because they exist as pure possibility. Unlike memories, which are fossils, long dead and buried deep."</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />First of all, the character development in this book is one of the best I've seen. The characters have so much depth to them at the end than when they were first introduced in the book. It's utterly brilliant how the author has managed to paint such complex, yet relatable characters, with all their struggles and hardships and yet not making them too monotonous. I love when books explore the relationship of teenagers with their parents, I feel so many books fail to explore this aspect of teenage life. Henry's relationship with his mom, his grandma and his brother is a thing to be adored.<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>" Sometimes I think gravity may be death in disguise. Other times I think gravity is love, which is why love's only demand is that we fall."</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />I think I say this a lot, but I love it when the writing style of a book is so captivating. I will take a well-written character driven book over a plot heavy book anyday. This was one of them. The book has so much grief in it and yet the author manages to keep the readers from being overwhelmed by introducing humor into the book. Just in the right amounts, so that it provides a relief from all the heavy themes. This book would be a nightmare for someone who wishes to annotate. There are so many wonderful quotes and passages in this book, so good luck with that!<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>" Dreams are hopeful because they exist as pure possibility. Unlike memories, which are fossils, long dead and buried deep."</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />Don't think I sobbed over a book as much I did on this. There is this one moment in the book where the grandma (who is suffering from dementia) burns the Thanksgiving turkey and the the family members are all pissed off. The old woman holding on to her grandson's arm and with tears in her eyes says "I'm sorry, I just wanted to help." I kept the book aside and balled for a good five minutes or so, as I thought of my own grandma, she passed away a couple of years ago and even during her worse days, she always made sure she was helping the people in the family, helping mom with the food and things in general. I didn't even realize halfway through the book, how relatable I found Henry.<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>" Because you can only die once, but you can suffer forever"</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />i’m genuinely at a loss for words right now, although I just wrote a lot already, but I feel I can't praise this enough. This book was so much more than I was expecting. It really was introspective and philosophical. It dealt with a lot of heavy topics that i really wasn’t anticipating. I would recommend this book to everyone. Read this book! It is brilliant and you won't regret!<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>" We remember the past, live in the present, and write the future."</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13712464183849443979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2251724959" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251724959" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251724959?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251724959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11185832745997689874">TW: Suicide, self harm (mention), nihilism, severe bullying & physical assault, attempted rape<br/><br/>This book was refreshingly funny and raw—and not the type of male narrative that’s too crude or uncomfortable. However, the more it went on, the more flaws I began to notice.<br/><br/>First of all, I loved Henry's story. It's a mental health plot confined in this weird sci-fi/contemporary hybrid, and even though it's really open-ended, it somehow works. I like the philosophy of "Is the world worth saving?" from t</span>
  <span id="freeText11185832745997689874" style="display:none">TW: Suicide, self harm (mention), nihilism, severe bullying &amp; physical assault, attempted rape<br /><br />This book was refreshingly funny and raw—and not the type of male narrative that’s too crude or uncomfortable. However, the more it went on, the more flaws I began to notice.<br /><br />First of all, I loved Henry's story. It's a mental health plot confined in this weird sci-fi/contemporary hybrid, and even though it's really open-ended, it somehow works. I like the philosophy of "Is the world worth saving?" from the perspective of a depressed teen, and this book is a great reminder of seeing perspective. Although this concept is neat, it isn't entirely new &amp; revolutionary to me. Regardless, Henry's inner turmoil often brought tears to my eyes.<br /><br />Usually when there’s severe bullying in a YA book I find it just a bit exaggerated because it’s outside my experience, but this hit me so hard. I had to put the book down at certain points to hold back tears and fight through my anger for Marcus and all the other assholes in his school. At one point I was listening to music while reading this and Car Radio came on and I just had to stop and cry. It’s all too much. I wrote this paragraph when I was only 200 pages into the book, though, and I will say that some of the bullying elements did start to straddle the line of being unrealistic. (basically, Henry gets beat up a TON in this book)<br /><br />It's an emotional and impactful read, and yet there were times that I was ready for it to be done. I have a ~thing~ about YA contemporary books that are over 400 pages, because I just hit a wall and start skim reading parts I don't care about. In this, some dialogue is cliché and some of the characters would have the conversation three or four times in different settings/variations. Some parts to it just felt so randomly fitted in, like entire subplots that hinted at having significance but didn't really wrap up nicely. And that was also a disappointment--the ending is so abrupt. <br /><br />So although it's a nice story and I thought the sci-fi elements folded into it nicely and created a good metaphor for depression, I felt it lost some of its power in the repetitiveness/length/unoriginality of it. It stands out amongst other contemporaries, but even writing this review I already feel it losing some of its luster that I noticed as I read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11185832745997689874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1943941487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1943941487" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1943941487?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481475204" href="/book/show/27220730-we-are-the-ants">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=psycho">psycho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943941487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1331557855808098691"><b>Maybe 4.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“We may not get to choose how we die, but we can choose how we live.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Well that was certainly a different kind of read. It’s familiar and new at the same time. Even though the themes are very common- bullying, mental illness, depression, broken family, search for identity and life’s meaning, all these things were manipulated and twisted into something new when the author brilliantly thought of throwing in the element of science in the story. The premise is actually pretty hila</span>
  <span id="freeText1331557855808098691" style="display:none"><b>Maybe 4.5 stars </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“We may not get to choose how we die, but we can choose how we live.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Well that was certainly a different kind of read. It’s familiar and new at the same time. Even though the themes are very common- bullying, mental illness, depression, broken family, search for identity and life’s meaning, all these things were manipulated and twisted into something new when the author brilliantly thought of throwing in the element of science in the story. The premise is actually pretty hilarious. I was laughing really hard at the clever idea. Leave the fate of earthlings in the hands of an angsty teenage boy (who lives a particularly miserable life) when he has been given by the aliens (who regularly abduct him since he was little) two choices: press the red button and the world doesn’t end, do not press it and the world ends. Good luck, world! <br /><br /> Anyone who reads this will tear through the pages if only to find out what Henry chooses in the end and regardless of whether the red button is metaphorical or literal, any reader will just have to know. But honestly, I enjoyed the novel for many other reasons. The writing is impressively natural, insightful, philosophical, and sometimes morbid but a lot of times very funny and relatable. Take a peek:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It’s comforting to know that regardless of our vast differences and the light-years that separate our worlds, we’ll always have nipples in common.” </i>
</b>(lol!)<br /><br />I particularly enjoyed the chapters where Henry visualizes hundreds of different ways the world could possibly end. It was really impressive how the author managed to come up with a good YA contemporary story diversified by science and very well-developed characters that I often try to put myself in their shoes because they’re that relatable. I wasn’t very keen on this line though <b>
  <i>“Books are for ugly people.” </i>
</b> and on the ending of the story (because somehow, I still want more) but I think it’s still as good as it could get.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1331557855808098691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's a battle you fight every day. You never stop, never get to rest. It's one bloody fray after another.</blockquote><br />4.5/5 🌟!<br /><br />When I tell you I read We Are the Ants at the perfect time, I'm not being hyperbolic. I read this at a tremulous and shaky point, where I understood the heavy emotions radiating from this book and from every word written because I lived and still am living in it. It probably wasn't the wisest choice to read such a book last year while I was sensitive to the topic of depression and mental health but it really helped me feel like I was one hundred percent seen and understood. <br /><br />Some parts (<i>ahem, take a shot every time dicks are mentioned</i><br />It was beautiful and brutally honest. It's a book that will stay with me forever because even months later, I still have a visceral reaction to Hutchinson's prose and his bare honesty about humanity.<br /><br />•— •— •— •— •— •— •— •— •— •— •— •— •—<br /><br />goodreads: you finished we are the ants. what next?<br />me: uhm i'm a mess of emotions, i don't know what's next ! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17917095551484661688"><b>“We may not get to choose how we die, but we can chose how we live. <br/>The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on.” <br/>― Shaun David Hutchinson, We Are the Ants</b><br/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516222114ra/24888896.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4.5/5</b><br/>Oh my gosh this book made me cry my eyes out. I felt every emotion on the planet while reading it. I’m actually struggling to write this review because I don’t know how to put my feelings into physical words. Not only was the way the story unfolded different and interesting, so w</span>
  <span id="freeText17917095551484661688" style="display:none"><b>“We may not get to choose how we die, but we can chose how we live. <br>The universe may forget us, but it doesn't matter. Because we are the ants, and we'll keep marching on.” <br>― Shaun David Hutchinson, We Are the Ants</b><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516222114ra/24888896.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4.5/5</b><br>Oh my gosh this book made me cry my eyes out. I felt every emotion on the planet while reading it. I’m actually struggling to write this review because I don’t know how to put my feelings into physical words. Not only was the way the story unfolded different and interesting, so were the characters. <br>Meet Henry Denton, a teenage boy who is regularly abducted by aliens, he also has to make a choice. The world will end in 144 days, and all he has to do to stop it is push a big red button, but Henry isn't your typical protagonist, he hates his life, and has been dealing with depression, bullying, abuse and grieve for years, so why would he want to save anything about a planet where people can be so evil.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1zpOKojAy9VPI/dJV/+2jTVupZltcgJQd+fuMhFrwTQt8fSPmuXo2r6XU4d0YPcixla0aacHQuDHnz2bSOTYfg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9UUhv6e4EKPhRdE9hmmjLCgcX8i+xGxcQmJAFJUqURYPjpsatZ0zrBDxdfOl9uKD2yROOHSxLOzyGpO9zKVIXA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1836752723268760855">Shaun is a major geek and all about nerdy shenanigans. He is the author of many queer books for young adults. Find out more information at shaundavidhutchinson.com. He currently lives in Seattle and watches way too much Doctor Who.</span>
